### Cajal-Retzius cell `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695`
#### Removed
- [Cajal-Retzius cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A neuron of the human embryonic marginal zone which display, as a salient feature, radial ascending processes that contact the pial surface, and a horizontal axon plexus located in the deep marginal zone. One feature of these cells in mammals is that they express the Reelin gene."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:10600995"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:9728912"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Cajal-Retzius cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695) SubClassOf [central nervous system neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000029) 

- [Cajal-Retzius cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695) SubClassOf [RO_0002100](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/RO_0002100) some [UBERON_0010403](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/UBERON_0010403) 

#### Added
- [Cajal-Retzius cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A type of transient, early-born glutamatergic neuron located primarily in the marginal zone (future layer I) of the developing cerebral cortex and hippocampus in vertebrates. it is characterized by a bipolar morphology with an elongated soma, a single thick dendrite oriented toward the pial surface, and a long, thin axon that extends tangentially to form horizontal plexuses across the cortical surface. It is important for the multiple developmental processes including migration, dendritogenesis and synaptogenesis. It typically undergoes programmed cell death following cortical maturation with species- and region specific patterns of survival. In mice, it is predominantly observed in the hippocampal formation, particularly in the stratum lacunosum-moleculare and outer molecular layer of the dentate gyrus (van Bruggen et al., 2023). In contrast, in humans, a second morphologically distinct subpopulation emerges mid-gestation and persists postnatally, with surviving cells observed in the cortical sulci and the hippocampus."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:36774666"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:10600995"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:9728912"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:37775311"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:34047341"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Cajal-Retzius cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000695) SubClassOf [glutamatergic neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000679)

### Merkel cell `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000242`
#### Removed
- [Merkel cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000242) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A modified epidermal cell located in the stratum basale. They are found mostly in areas where sensory perception is acute. Merkel cells are closely associated with an expanded terminal bulb of an afferent myelinated nerve fiber."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "MESH:D018862"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [Merkel cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000242) SubClassOf [BFO_0000050](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/BFO_0000050) some [UBERON_0002025](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/UBERON_0002025) 

- [Merkel cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000242) SubClassOf [keratinocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000312) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:19782676"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

#### Added
- [Merkel cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000242) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A specialized epithelial cell located in the skin epidermis and certain mucosal epithelia. It functions as a mechanoreceptor for light touch by forming synapse-like contacts with somatosensory afferent nerve endings, contributing to slowly adapting type I (SAI) tactile responses. Characterized by dense-core neuroendocrine granules, the Merkel cell exhibits both sensory and neuroendocrine properties, including regulated neurotransmitter release via SNARE complex-dependent mechanisms. Its development in mice depends on the transcription factor Atoh1."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:19834574"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:24862916"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "MESH:D018862"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:30415995"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:2274847"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "Wikipedia:Merkel_cell"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [cerebellar basket cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000027) [depiction](http://xmlns.com/foaf/0.1/depiction) [CB_circuits_PMID3650468_f2.png](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/cl/images/CB_circuits_PMID3650468_f2.png) 
  - [license](http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/license) "https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-nd/4.0/"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "doi:10.1016/j.cnp.2022.11.002"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cerebellar basket cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000027) [depiction](http://xmlns.com/foaf/0.1/depiction) [Candelabrum_cell.png](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/Candelabrum_cell.png) 
  - [license](http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/license) "https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-nd/4.0/"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "doi:10.3389/fnins.2020.00293"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cerebellar basket cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000027) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A GABAergic inhibitory interneuron located in the molecular layer of the cerebellar cortex. It projects axons that form specialized synaptic structures around Purkinje cells, including pericellular baskets, which wrap around the Purkinje cell soma, and the pinceau: a brush-like terminal that contacts the initial segment of the Purkinje cell axon. The basket cell modulates Purkinje cell activity through both chemical (GABAergic) and non-synaptic (ephaptic) mechanisms. It is arranged in sagittal rows that align with Purkinje cell zones, contributing to the cerebellum's modular and topographically organized architecture. It plays an essential role in regulating motor coordination and potentially cognitive functions."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:8915580"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:32990595"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cerebellar basket cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000027) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "cerebellar basket cell"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [cerebellar basket cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_2000027) SubClassOf [molecular layer interneuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4042035)

### chandelier pvalb GABAergic cortical interneuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023036`
#### Removed
- [chandelier pvalb GABAergic cortical interneuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023036) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "The marker set GPR149, CA8 can identify the Human cell type chandelier pvalb GABAergic cortical interneuron in the Brain with a confidence of 0.799748111 (NS-Forest FBeta value). In mice, Chandelier PV cells have soma found in in upper L2/3, with some in deep L5 and exhibit fast-spiking but lower firing rate compared to basket cells, and have practically absent hyperpolarization sag."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:27477017"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.11165918"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

#### Added
- [chandelier pvalb GABAergic cortical interneuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023036) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "In mice, Chandelier PV cells have soma found in in upper L2/3, with some in deep L5 and exhibit fast-spiking but lower firing rate compared to basket cells, and have practically absent hyperpolarization sag. The marker set GPR149, CA8 can identify the Human cell type chandelier pvalb GABAergic cortical interneuron in the neocortex with a confidence of 0.799748111 (NS-Forest FBeta value)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### granular cell of epidermis `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002189`
#### Removed
- [granular cell of epidermis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002189) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A keratinocyte of the epidermis that is characterized by containing granules of keratohyalin and lamellar granules."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "ISBN:1416031855"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

#### Added
- [granular cell of epidermis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002189) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A keratinocyte located in the stratum granulosum of the epidermis, characterized by the presence of keratohyalin granules containing filaggrin&mdash;which aggregate keratin filament &mdash;and by lamellar granules that secrete lipids and enzymes essential for forming the skin&rsquo;s waterproof barrier. As these cells progress toward the surface, they adopt a flattened morphology and initiate keratinization to become corneocyte and form the protective stratum corneum. In human epidermis, granular keratinocytes are transcriptomically distinguished by high expression of differentiation markers such as DSC1, KRT2, IVL, and TGM3 (Wang et al., 2020), and LOR, FLG, and SPINK5 (Cheng et al., 2018)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### hypothalamic gonadotropin-releasing hormone neuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0011111`
#### Removed
- [hypothalamic gonadotropin-releasing hormone neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0011111) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A neuroendocrine cell that secretes gonadotropin-releasing hormone (GnRH). A GnRH neuron is born in the nasal placode during embryonic development and migrates through the nose and forebrain to the hypothalamus. This cell regulates reproduction by secreting GnRH into the pituitary portal vessels to induce the release of gonadotropins into the general circulation."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:21828096"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "GOC:NV"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [hypothalamic gonadotropin-releasing hormone neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0011111) [label](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label) "gonadotropin-releasing hormone neuron"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

#### Added
- [hypothalamic gonadotropin-releasing hormone neuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0011111) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "a specialized neuroendocrine cell that synthesizes and secretes GnRH decapeptide, a key regulator of reproductive function. It originates from the olfactory placode during embryonic development and migrates into the forebrain where it localises predominantly in the hypothalamus and in humans, in extrahypothalamic regions like the basal ganglia (Skrapits et al., 2021). This cell regulates reproduction by secreting GnRH into the pituitary portal vessels to induce the release of gonadotropins into the general circulation. It expresses receptor subunits required for AMPA, NMDA, and kainate receptor signaling and may use glutamate as a neurotransmitter in recurrent collateral innervation."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:26053743"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

  - [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "Schematic of the conventional outflow pathway, showing the Schlemm's canal (SC, green) and the trabecular meshwork (TM, orange). The left inset shows an expanded view of the Schlemm&rsquo;s canal&rsquo;s microanatomy detailing the cell morphology of the inner and outer wall endocrine cells. The inner wall endocrine cells, shown in blue, line the canal surface facing the trabecular meshwork. Some of the inner wall cells contain giant vacuoles."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [inner wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033098) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A Schlemm's canal endothelial cell that lines the inner wall of the Schlemm's canal. This cell exhibits a cobblestone appearance due to the significant biomechanical load it experiences, as well as the segmental flow of aqueous humor. The degree of biomechanical stress can lead to the formation of dome-like outpouchings known as giant vacuoles. In addition, the cell contains transcellular pores that mediate aqueous humor transport (Dautriche et al., 2015). This endothelial cell also displays prominent peripheral F-actin bands which help maintain structural integrity under pressure (Ethier et al., 2004)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:15454474"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### mature myelinating oligodendrocyte `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072003`

#### Added
- Class: [mature myelinating oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072003) 

- [mature myelinating oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072003) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0002-5507-2103](https://orcid.org/0000-0002-5507-2103) 

- [mature myelinating oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072003) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4072003"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [mature myelinating oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072003) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A post-mitotic oligodendrocyte derived from a myelin-forming oligodendrocyte (MFOL). A mature Myelinating Oligodendrocyte is a fully differentiated cell that is actively engaged in myelination. In addition to high expression of canonical myelin genes (e.g., Mbp, Plp1, Mog), a MOL can be distinguished by the expression of stage-enriched genes Grm3, Klk6, Ptgds, Anxa5, and Hopx in mice. These markers reflect the functional specialization of a mature oligodendrocyte, including roles in signalling, lipid metabolism, and myelin maintenance."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:27284195"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:33203872"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### multiciliated columnar cell of tracheobronchial tree `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002145`
#### Removed
- [multiciliated columnar cell of tracheobronchial tree](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002145) [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "https://cellxgene.cziscience.com/cellguide/CL_0002145"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [multiciliated columnar cell of tracheobronchial tree](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002145) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "The marker set C1orf194, MS4A8 can identify the Human cell type ciliated columnar cell of tracheobronchial tree in the Lung with a confidence of 0.86 (NS-Forest FBeta value). These cells possess numerous cilia on their surface, typically ranging from 200 to 300 per cell. The cilia vary in length, measuring between 6 to 7 &mu;m in the upper airways (trachea) and becoming shorter, around 4 &mu;m, in the smaller airways (terminal bronchioles). These cells form a two-layered 'coat' in the airway: the lower 'sol' layer is watery, allowing the cilia to beat in coordinated waves, while the upper 'gel' layer is thick and sticky, trapping inhaled particles."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "https://doi.org/10.1016/B978-032304048-8.50071-2"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

These cells possess numerous cilia on their surface, typically ranging from 200 to 300 per cell. The cilia vary in length, measuring between 6 to 7 &mu;m in the upper airways (trachea) and becoming shorter, around 4 &mu;m, in the smaller airways (terminal bronchioles). ### myelin-forming oligodendrocyte `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002`

#### Added
- Class: [myelin-forming oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002) 

- [myelin-forming oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0002-5507-2103](https://orcid.org/0000-0002-5507-2103) 

- [myelin-forming oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4072002"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [myelin-forming oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A postmitotic and differentiated oligodendrocyte derived from a oligodendrocyte progenitor cell. A myelin-forming oligodendrocyte begins the expression of myelin genes and actively engages in the myelination process. In mice and humans, it is characterized by the upregulation of the key myelin-associated markers Mbp and Opalin. Additionally, Ctps (CTP synthase) shows peak expression at this stage, suggesting a heightened demand for nucleotide biosynthesis during membrane expansion and myelin production."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:39233334"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:27284195"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:9473608"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:30837646"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [myelin-forming oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072002) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "MFOL"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [has_synonym_type](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasSynonymType) [OMO_0003000](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/OMO_0003000) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:39233334"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### newly formed oligodendrocyte `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001`

#### Added
- Class: [newly formed oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001) 

- [newly formed oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0002-5507-2103](https://orcid.org/0000-0002-5507-2103) 

- [newly formed oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4072001"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [newly formed oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A post-mitotic oligodendrocyte that has exited the cell cycle and begun early stage differentiation. The cell begins to acquire oligodendrocyte-like characteristics but has not yet initiated myelination. In mice, NFOL is marked by the expression of Tcf7l2 and Cemip2 (also known as Tmem2), among other early myelin-related genes. These markers highlight cells transitioning from a precursor to a more differentiated, pre-myelinating state."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:39233334"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:27284195"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [newly formed oligodendrocyte](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072001) [has_related_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasRelatedSynonym) "NFOL"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [has_synonym_type](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasSynonymType) [OMO_0003000](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/OMO_0003000)

This cell originates from multiple structures within the developing brain including the medial ganglion eminence and the lateral ganglionic eminence. These cells migrate throughout the central nervous system and persist into adulthood where they play an important role in remyelination of injured neurons."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

#### Added
- [oligodendrocyte precursor cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0002453) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A proliferative and migratory glial progenitor cell that derives from a neural stem cell and resides within the central nervous system. It possesses the capacity to differentiate into a committed oligodendrocyte progenitor (COP) through a well-defined series of maturation steps, ultimately giving rise to a myelinating oligodendrocyte (MOL). In mice and humans, it is characterized by the expression of specific molecular markers, including Pdgfra, Cspg4 (also known as NG2) and Olig2."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099`

#### Added

- [outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099) [contributor](http://purl.org/dc/terms/contributor) [0000-0001-6677-8489](https://orcid.org/0000-0001-6677-8489) 

- [outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099) [date](http://purl.org/dc/terms/date) "2025-06-17T13:33:41Z"^^[dateTime](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#dateTime) 

- [outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4033099"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099) [depiction](http://xmlns.com/foaf/0.1/depiction) "http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/cl/images/Schlemms_canal_endo_cell_PMID26402712.png"^^[anyURI](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#anyURI) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:26402712"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "Schematic of the conventional outflow pathway, showing the Schlemm's canal (SC, green) and the trabecular meshwork (TM, orange). The left inset shows an expanded view of the Schlemm&rsquo;s canal&rsquo;s microanatomy detailing the cell morphology of the inner and outer wall endocrine cells. The outer wall endocrine cells, shown in green, line the side of Schlemm&rsquo;s canal facing the collector channels and venous system."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [license](http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/license) "http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [outer wall Schlemm's canal endothelial cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033099) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A Schlemm's canal endothelial cell that lines the outer wall of the Schlemm's canal. This cell displays a smooth and flat morphology (Dautriche et al., 2015) and it is distinguished by the presence of Weibel-Palade bodies, specialized organelles that produce, store, and release P-Selectin (Hamanaka et al., 1992). This endothelial cell also exhibits stellate (star-shaped) actin arrangements distributed throughout much of the cell (Ethier et al., 2004)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:15454474"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

#### Removed
- [respiratory tract suprabasal cell](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4033048) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "The marker set TNC, KRT15, SERPINB4 can identify the Human cell type respiratory suprabasal cell in the Lung with a confidence of 0.62 (NS-Forest FBeta value). In humans, respiratory tract suprabasal cells have been noted to have enriched expression of the following: CK8, KRT13, IVL, and SERPINB3. Single-cell sequencing indicates that suprabasal cells derived from the nasal epithelium are distinct from those in the tracheobronchial epithelium."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### spinous cell of epidermis `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000649`
#### Removed
- [spinous cell of epidermis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000649) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "prickle cell of epidermis"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [spinous cell of epidermis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000649) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A cell with delicate radiating processes known as desmosomes that form intercellular bridges between other cells of this type. This cell type forms the stratum spinosum (prickle cell layer). A function of this cell is to generate keratin."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "ISBN:0815332181"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

#### Added
- [spinous cell of epidermis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_0000649) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A keratinocyte found within the stratum spinosum (prickle cell layer) of the epidermis, distinguished by numerous intercellular desmosomes, which give it a &ldquo;prickly&rdquo; or spiny appearance. Positioned above the mitotically active basal layer and beneath the granular layer, it contributes to the skin&rsquo;s mechanical strength and barrier function, preventing water loss and pathogen entry. This cell expresses differentiation-specific keratins K1 and K10 in mice, unlike basal cells that express K5 and K14, and lacks the keratohyalin granules found in granular cells, marking its intermediate stage of epidermal differentiation."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "ISBN:0815332181"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "GOC:tfm"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

### sst GABAergic cortical interneuron `http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023017`
#### Removed
- [sst GABAergic cortical interneuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023017) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "In the mouse cortex, sst GABAergic cortical interneurons show heterogeneous electrophysiological signatures varying between low-threshold spiking (LTS), regular-spiking and fast-spiking (Song, Y. H., Yoon, J., &amp; Lee, S. H. 2021). Sst GABAergic cortical interneurons have multiple functional roles in the brain. In the mouse, they involved in the generation of slow-waves during the sleep phase of non-rapid eye-movement (NREM) (Funk, C. M. et al., 2017), they maintain synaptic plasticity during motor learning (Adler, A., Zhao, R., et al., 2021), they enhance visual perception in the V1 cortical area by suppressing the activity of pyramidal excitatory neurons (Song, YH. et al., 2020). In humans, malfunctioning of sst GABAergic cortical interneurons is associated with neurodegenerative and psychiatric disorders such as Parkinson's disease, Alzheimer's disease, major depressive disorder, bipolar disorder and schizophrenia as individuals affected by these pathologies show a decrease of expression of SST in the brain (Song YH., Yoon J. et al., 2021). The marker set SST, PLCH1 can identify the Human cell type sst GABAergic cortical interneuron in the Brain with a confidence of 0.842367005 (NS-Forest FBeta value)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:32494634"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.11165918"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:30792151"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:28821651"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

#### Added
- [sst GABAergic cortical interneuron](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4023017) [comment](http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#comment) "In the mouse cortex, sst GABAergic cortical interneurons show heterogeneous electrophysiological signatures varying between low-threshold spiking (LTS), regular-spiking and fast-spiking (Song, Y. H., Yoon, J., &amp; Lee, S. H. 2021). Sst GABAergic cortical interneurons have multiple functional roles in the brain. In the mouse, they involved in the generation of slow-waves during the sleep phase of non-rapid eye-movement (NREM) (Funk, C. M. et al., 2017), they maintain synaptic plasticity during motor learning (Adler, A., Zhao, R., et al., 2021), they enhance visual perception in the V1 cortical area by suppressing the activity of pyramidal excitatory neurons (Song, YH. et al., 2020). In humans, malfunctioning of sst GABAergic cortical interneurons is associated with neurodegenerative and psychiatric disorders such as Parkinson's disease, Alzheimer's disease, major depressive disorder, bipolar disorder and schizophrenia as individuals affected by these pathologies show a decrease of expression of SST in the brain (Song YH., Yoon J. et al., 2021). The marker set SST, PLCH1 can identify the Human cell type sst GABAergic cortical interneuron in the neocortex with a confidence of 0.842367005 (NS-Forest FBeta value)."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:32494634"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)

- [tanycyte of vascular organ of lamina terminalis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072014) [id](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#id) "CL:4072014"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [tanycyte of vascular organ of lamina terminalis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072014) [has_broad_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasBroadSynonym) "Tanycyte-like cells in CVOs"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:23649873"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [tanycyte of vascular organ of lamina terminalis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072014) [definition](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115) "A specialized, non-ciliated ependymal glial cell located in the ventricular wall of the organum vasculosum of the lamina terminalis (OVLT) and characterized by elongated basal processes extending into the parenchyma to contact fenestrated capillaries. In mice, it is characterised by the expression of tight junction proteins (claudin 1, occludin, ZO-1) forming a continuous honeycomb junctional pattern. This cell contributes to a functional blood&ndash;cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) barrier at the ventricular interface of the OVLT."^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 
  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:23649873"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

  - [database_cross_reference](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref) "PMID:26017494"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string) 

- [tanycyte of vascular organ of lamina terminalis](http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CL_4072014) [has_exact_synonym](http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasExactSynonym) "tanycyte-like cell of OVLT"^^[string](http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#string)
